    "# Research Question"
   ]
  },
  {
   "cell_type": "markdown",
   "metadata": {
    "pycharm": {
     "name": "#%% md\n"
    }
   },
   "source": [
    "What internal demographic differences and events are present among displaced Syrian refugees? Does the relative political climates and demographics of host nations result effect the amount of Syrian Refugees fleeing to the specific nation?"
   ]
  },
  {
   "cell_type": "markdown",
   "metadata": {
    "pycharm": {
     "name": "#%% md\n"
    }
   },
   "source": [
    "<a id='background'></a>\n",
    "\n",
    "## Background & Prior Work"
   ]
  },
  {
   "cell_type": "markdown",
   "metadata": {
    "pycharm": {
     "name": "#%% md\n"
    }
   },
   "source": [
    "In the modern socio-political climate refugee and asylum seekers comprise one of the most vulnerable and one of the fastest growing populations. A 2021 study of refugee and asylum seekers by the United Nations indicated that a record number 84 million refugees had been displaced in the time period between January 2021 and November 2021 [^UN2]. Current projections show the effects of climate change, the COVID-19 Pandemic and governmental instability exacerbating this already growing trend throughout the 2020s. Understanding refugee patterns and the taken towards resettlement is key to being properly prepared and integrating them into host countries. Representing the largest and longest refugee crisis of the 2010s, an analysis of refugee data from the Syrian Civil War can provide insights on how governments and NGOs can better prepare for future global crises.\n",
    "\n",
    "Following the most intense drought in modern Syrian history from 2006 to 2010, the largely agrarian population had resettled into urban ghettos. Following the period of resettlement, disturbed populations began to protest inequitable economic policy as well as the complacent Assad regime [^Brit]. Military response to the peaceful protests seen throughout the region sparked what has become a decade long civil war for control of Syria. The Civil War has seen over 6.6 million registered Syrian refugees leave the country [^UN].\n",
    "\n",
    "References:\n",
    "[^Brit]: Britannica, The Editors of Encyclopaedia. \"Syrian Civil War\". *Encyclopedia Britannica*, 17 Jul. 2020, https://www.britannica.com/event/Syrian-Civil-War. Accessed 21 April 2022.\n",
    "[^UN]: “Syria Refugee Crisis Explained.” How to Help Refugees - Aid, Relief and Donations, 2021, https://www.unrefugees.org/news/syria-refugee-crisis-explained/#What%20is%20happening%20in%20Syria’s%20northwest%20region%20–%C2%A0specifically%20in%20Idlib%C2%A0–%C2%A0right%20now?\n",
    "[^UN2]: “2021 Year in Review: Refugee, Migrant Numbers Rise, despite Travel Curbs | | UN News.” United Nations, United Nations, 2021, https://www.news.un.org/en/story/2021/12/1108472.\n"
   ]
  },

   "source": [
    "# Hypothesis\n"
   ]
  },
  {
   "cell_type": "markdown",
   "metadata": {
    "pycharm": {
     "name": "#%% md\n"
    }
   },
   "source": [
    "Our team believes that refugees of the Syrian civil war will be skewed towards women, children, and the elderly. We believe that conscription and pressure to volunteer will result in men ages 18-35 remaining in the country. Furthermore we believe that politically calm and more stable nations will attract more refugees than other nations. While they are ultimately looking to flee from prosecution to relative safety, social programs and political stability will attract refugees more than instability."

    "# Data Cleaning"
   ]
  },
  {
   "cell_type": "markdown",
   "metadata": {
    "pycharm": {
     "name": "#%% md\n"
    }
   },
   "source": [
    "We obtained our datasets from public data sites including the ACLED and data2. All datasets used had varying numbers of observations and attributes. The data provided by ACLED had many columns that we as a group deemed not necessary or usable for our data analysis. Because of this we decided to patch together specific tables that included only the event date, event type, country, and number of fatalities for a given event. This data was already saved in a csv file, so we only had to upload it to the repo in order to access it. Afterwards, we checked if there were any null values within the dataframe. None were present.\n",
    "\n",
    "For the dataset including the total persons of concern by country of asylum, the site that we pulled the data from did not have an accessible csv file. Because of this, we had to access the data as JSON and then use a JSON to csv converter, where we were then able to download and load in the data. Similar to the data we obtained from ACLED, there were many columns that were not necessary for our analysis, so we created a subset of the dataframe which reduced it from 78 columns to 2. Following that, we dropped the observations for nations not bordering Syria (Egypt, Northern African nations, etc). Lastly, we added a new column to this dataframe called \"Benefits\", referring to the existence legal frameworks available to Syrian Refugees. This included programs allowing refugees to obtain citizenship and other benefits offered by host countries. We obtained this data by looking into which countries were signatories of the 1951 Refugee Convention, a legal framework for refugee rights. We quantified the legal framework by assigning the value of 1 to countries that were signatories, and 0 to countries that were not.\n",
    "\n",
    "Furthermore, the dataset including different age groups and genders was also pulled from data2 which did not have an accessible csv file, so we once again used a converter. When we loaded in the data, we noticed that there was only 1 row and 109 columns. Because the data was formatted like this, we rearranged the data so that Male and Female were the observations (rows), and the different age groups were the columns. We also dropped the unnecessary columns. Several column names were not easy to read, so we renamed them to make them more intuitive. Lastly, we took the totals among the rows and created a new column with the total values."
   ]

    "Unsurprisingly, Syrian refugees ages between 18 and 59 consisted the highest number in both genders due to the large age range being grouped here. However, if we look specifically at age groups below 18 and combine the three age groups, you can notice that it is almost just as much as the \"18 to 59\" age group, accounting about 46 and 48 percent of the total refugee population in both males and females respectively. This signifies that children and teenagers make up a significant portion of the refugees, almost half of the refugee population.\n",

    "# distribution of males and females per country\n",
    "male_female = reduce(lambda  left,right: pd.merge(left,right,on=['country'],\n",
    "                                            how='outer'), [male, female])\n",
    "male_female = pd.melt(male_female, id_vars='country', value_vars=['male', 'female'])\n",
    "\n",
    "# distribution of event types\n",
    "sns.set(style = \"white\")\n",
    "\n",
    "# figure size in inches\n",
    "rcParams['figure.figsize'] = 16, 8\n",
    "\n",
    "male_female_visual = sns.barplot(x = 'country', y = 'value', hue = 'variable', data = male_female)\n",
    "male_female_visual.set_title('Population of Males and Females per Country', fontsize=16)\n",
    "male_female_visual.set_ylabel('Count')\n",
    "male_female_visual.grid(axis = 'y')"
   ]

    "Although the life expectancies of all of the countries are relatively similar, the mortality rates of those under 5 years old are extremely stark. Turkey and Iraq have rates over 20% whereas Jordan and Lebanon have rates under 20%. Taking a deeper look into the life expectancies, people in Iraq and Turkey  have lower life expectancies than Jordan and Lebanon. This indicates that Iraq and Turkey may have less healthy populations than Jordan and Lebanon.\n",

    "                                            how='outer'), [unemployment, inflation])\n",
    "unemployment_inflation = pd.melt(unemployment_inflation, id_vars='country', value_vars=['unemployment', 'inflation'])\n",
    "\n",
    "sns.set(style = \"white\")\n",
    "\n",
    "# figure size in inches\n",
    "rcParams['figure.figsize'] = 16, 8\n",
    "\n",
    "unemployment_inflation_visual = sns.barplot(x = 'country', y = 'value', hue = 'variable', data = unemployment_inflation)\n",
    "unemployment_inflation_visual.set_title('Rates of Unemployment and Inflation per Country', fontsize=16)\n",
    "unemployment_inflation_visual.set_ylabel('Percentage')\n",
    "unemployment_inflation_visual.grid(axis = 'y')"
   ]

    "## Data Analysis Game Plan (incomplete)\n",
    "1) correlation matrix to see if any of the variables are highly correlated\n",
    "\n",
    "\"\"\"\n",
    "ex:\n",
    "Variable Correlation\n",
    "\n",
    "Another important thing to understand when exploring data sets is the correlation between variables. One statistical tool we can use for this is the Pearson Correlation. For this EDA, our team has created the following heat map, which clearly designates variable pairings with the associated correlation values.\n",
    "\n",
    "1.0 means complete correlation - something only found when a variable is correlated with itself.\n",
    "\n",
    "#Using Pearson Correlation\n",
    "df_corr = eda_df[['rating','script_num_words','number_of_profanities','number_deaths','avg_death_importance','num_main_char_deaths','num_love_scenes']]\n",
    "plt.figure(figsize=(8,8))\n",
    "cor = df_corr.corr().sort_values(['rating'],ascending=False)\n",
    "cor = cor[cor.index]\n",
    "sns.heatmap(cor, annot=True, cmap=plt.cm.Reds)\n",
    "plt.show()\n",
    "\"\"\"\n",
    "\n",
    "2) feature selection (if needed)\n",
    "\n",
    "3) ml model -- decision tree, k-nearest neighbors, \"Linear SVM\", \"RBF SVM\", \"Gaussian Process\", \"Random Forest\", \"Neural Net\", \"AdaBoost\", \"Naive Bayes\", \"QDA\"\n",
    "\n",
    "\"\"\"\n",
    "svm discussion\n",
    "“Support Vector Machines” (SVM) is a supervised learning technique as it gets trained using sample dataset. SVM is complex under the hood while figuring out higher dimensional support vectors or referred as hyperplanes across which to divide the data forming different clusters.\n",
    "SVM provides user to choose different kernel functions (or clustering/classification algorithms) to get better results for specific dataset nature. There are various kernel options available like “linear” (which is linear regression technique), “poly” (for nonlinear or polynomial regression), “rbf” etc. For things like polynomial SVC (Support Vector Classifier) right degree polynomial is required to be used to tune for better results.\n",
    "\"\"\""

    "# Ethics & Privacy"
   ]
  },
  {
   "cell_type": "code",
   "execution_count": null,
   "metadata": {
    "pycharm": {
     "name": "#%%\n"
    }
   },
   "outputs": [],
   "source": [
    "Our project is being done purely for academic purposes, and all of the datasets that we pull from are publicly available. Additionally, the entries from these datasets are unmodified, and are analyzed directly from the CSV files. We would also like to address that while we attempted to include as many factors that could potentially affect the resettlement relocation of Syrian refugees, we may be missing other factors that could have higher predictive values. This could have an unintended consequence of someone misusing our findings as they may not be completely comprehensive. Furthermore, these datasets are pulled from websites including UNICEF, UNHCR, and ACLED, in which the data should be confirmed before making any declarative statements or other assumptions as there may be inconsistencies.\n",
    "\n",
    "Additionally, there are also privacy concerns for those who view our project and want to access the datasets that we used. Some of these sites may collect personal information such as names, postal address, email addresses, telephone numbers, social media names, contact preferences, gender, date of birth, etc. While some sites may collect standard information such as an IP address or computer ID, others require the user to sign up and provide other details."
   ]
